  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_13b023eb-df3d-4cd6-9edf-40c266fccefe'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6489497817237861624"><b>A New York Times bestseller</b><br/><br/><b>A TIME Magazine Top 10 Children's Book of 2015</b><br/><br/>"<i>Saint Anything</i> is a poignant, honest story about how we might suffer the misfortune of someone else's bad choices, how people who love us can become family when we desperately need it, and how starting over might - miraculously - mean taking a solid leap forward." —<b>Jodi Picoult, New York Times bestse</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6489497817237861624" style="display:none"><b>A New York Times bestseller</b><br /><br /><b>A TIME Magazine Top 10 Children's Book of 2015</b><br /><br />"<i>Saint Anything</i> is a poignant, honest story about how we might suffer the misfortune of someone else's bad choices, how people who love us can become family when we desperately need it, and how starting over might - miraculously - mean taking a solid leap forward." —<b>Jodi Picoult, New York Times bestselling novelist of Leaving Time and My Sister’s Keeper</b><br /><br />Sydney has always felt invisible. She's grown accustomed to her brother, Peyton, being the focus of the family’s attention and, lately, concern. Peyton is handsome and charismatic, but seems bent on self-destruction. Now, after a drunk-driving accident that crippled a boy, Peyton’s serving some serious jail time, and Sydney is on her own, questioning her place in the family and the world.<br /><br />Then she meets the Chatham family. Drawn into their warm, chaotic circle, Sydney experiences unquestioning acceptance for the first time. There’s effervescent Layla, who constantly falls for the wrong guy, Rosie, who’s had her own fall from grace, and Mrs. Chatham, who even though ailing is the heart of the family. But it’s with older brother Mac—quiet, watchful, and protective—that Sydney finally feels seen, really seen, at last.<br /><br /><i>Saint Anything</i> is Sarah Dessen’s deepest and most psychologically probing novel yet, telling an engrossing story of a girl discovering friendship, love, and herself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6489497817237861624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">He was the single most unnerving character to me. The way he acted felt all too real; like a "family friend" that gives you the creeps but bothers no <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">He was the single most unnerving character to me. The way he acted felt all too real; like a "family friend" that gives you the creeps but bothers no one else so you second-guess your gut instinct. That is utterly terrifying to me, the gaslighting effect such a person can have.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1276038398?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1276038398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13444139457098607934">2 1/2 stars. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23009402.Saint_Anything' title='Saint Anything by Sarah Dessen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Saint Anything</a> is my first Sarah Dessen book, which may have been a mistake, but all I know is that this book is a perfect example of how to write great, natural dialogue, fleshed-out characters and relationships, and <b>never once make me feel a single emotion</b>.<br/><br/>Despite reading praise after praise about Sarah Dessen, I admit I've avoided her work because her stories just do not sound very compelling. But I finally decided to cast aside my reservations and try this - a great writer can m</span>
  <span id="freeText13444139457098607934" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23009402.Saint_Anything" title="Saint Anything by Sarah Dessen" rel="nofollow noopener">Saint Anything</a> is my first Sarah Dessen book, which may have been a mistake, but all I know is that this book is a perfect example of how to write great, natural dialogue, fleshed-out characters and relationships, and <b>never once make me feel a single emotion</b>.<br /><br />Despite reading praise after praise about Sarah Dessen, I admit I've avoided her work because her stories just do not sound very compelling. But I finally decided to cast aside my reservations and try this - a great writer can make any story interesting, right?<br /><br />Um, I'm not so sure. I'm rating up on this one because it's hard to deny that Dessen is a competent writer. The narrative flows smoothly and the everyday dialogue feels realistic - she captures the "voice" of teenage girls very well. <b>Every character is complex and developed</b>, complete with likes, dislikes, aspirations, hopes and quirks that make them uniquely themselves. Very few authors manage this to the extent that Dessen does.<br /><br />But where is the hook? Where is the drive to keep turning pages to find out what will happen to Sydney? To Peyton? To Mac and Layla? It's so so tame. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23009402.Saint_Anything" title="Saint Anything by Sarah Dessen" rel="nofollow noopener">Saint Anything</a> needs a good shot of drama, angst, tragedy or <i>something</i> in order to be more than an exercise in good character writing.<br /><br />Perhaps it will appeal more to readers who genuinely enjoy quiet stories about everyday people. <b>But I just didn't feel much concern for Sydney or Peyton</b>. Maybe it's because I've recently read books about people who are starving, discriminated against, consumed by grief, but I found it hard to be worried what would happen to a pretty, wealthy girl with loving parents and good friends.<br /><br />The story begins with Sydney's brother - Peyton - being sent to jail for crippling a boy while drunk-driving. Then the camera turns to Sydney, who has to deal with the subsequent horror of overprotective parents and concerned friends. It was honestly quite hard to pity her and I had to roll my eyes when the legal stuff put strain on funds and they had to sell the beach house they never used anyway (boo freaking hoo).<br /><br />The most interesting thing about this book (in my opinion) was the way Sydney was treated by her parents after Peyton's conviction. I thought it was realistic and unfair that her parents would suddenly put restrictions on Sydney to avoid the same thing happening again. Which, I suppose, is ultimately what this book is about - how someone can get caught up in and be affected by another person's actions.<br /><br /><b>The romance was sweet, but forgettable</b>. As I already mentioned, Mac was well-developed and fleshed-out, yet lacking any real spark of personality to make their romance one I would remember.<br /><br />In fact, what I think I will remember most about this book is the FOOD. Pizza and french fries and yum! If it made me feel one thing, then that was HUNGER.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13444139457098607934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1058029555?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1058029555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1373443583763954771"><b>3.5 stars</b> Because it's Sarah Dessen, this is a very pleasant read. But it's not what I'd consider one of her standouts, since it doesn't have moments that quietly hit you the way her best books do. Still, Mac and Sydney are cute together--Sarah writes the most wonderful everyday conversations about nothing and boys who manage to be appealing despite not doing anything particularly dramatic--and the brother-sister storyline ended well, even if it didn't quite have the tension or emotional impact </span>
  <span id="freeText1373443583763954771" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b> Because it's Sarah Dessen, this is a very pleasant read. But it's not what I'd consider one of her standouts, since it doesn't have moments that quietly hit you the way her best books do. Still, Mac and Sydney are cute together--Sarah writes the most wonderful everyday conversations about nothing and boys who manage to be appealing despite not doing anything particularly dramatic--and the brother-sister storyline ended well, even if it didn't quite have the tension or emotional impact that I think was intended. <br /><br />Additionally, I don't have beef with fictional parents too often, but the hyper-controlling mom storyline here dragged out way too long. <br /><br />So if you're a die-hard Dessen fan, just know this one's fine to pass the time, but it might not be one of your favorites. And if you're new to Dessen and like quieter contemporary YA that are about friendships and family and ordinary girls growing up (with a nice, healthy bit of swoon thrown in), you might want to start with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51737.The_Truth_About_Forever" title="The Truth About Forever by Sarah Dessen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Truth About Forever</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51738.Just_Listen" title="Just Listen by Sarah Dessen" rel="nofollow noopener">Just Listen</a>. I fell in love with her after those (and after reading everything she's published except for one book that I'm hoarding for a rainy day), and despite my middling feelings on this one, I'll still happily read anything she writes. <br /><br /><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher. </i><br /><br />P.S. Food craving warning! This book is gonna make you want to eat piles and piles of pizza and French fries. So be prepared.</span>

<div id="review_1958935402" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1958935402" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1958935402?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1958935402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14870999730025055621">It’s been close to five years since I last read a Sarah Dessen book. In my defence, she doesn’t publish them every year, but I guess I just forgot how enjoyable they truly are. <br/><br/>I had my reservations going into this novel, because the title made me think that there was going to be a huge amount of religion, which I prefer to stay away from, but religion is not one of the themes, fortunately for me. <br/><br/>Since I know what it’s like to have an older brother who gets into trouble, I connected with Sydney</span>
  <span id="freeText14870999730025055621" style="display:none">It’s been close to five years since I last read a Sarah Dessen book. In my defence, she doesn’t publish them every year, but I guess I just forgot how enjoyable they truly are. <br /><br />I had my reservations going into this novel, because the title made me think that there was going to be a huge amount of religion, which I prefer to stay away from, but religion is not one of the themes, fortunately for me. <br /><br />Since I know what it’s like to have an older brother who gets into trouble, I connected with Sydney more than I could have hoped to. While my brother never actually got sentenced for anything, he did do some, pardon my language, stupid things, just like Peyton did. <br /><br />Except Peyton actually paralyzed a guy, so now he has to do prison time. It’s not just that Sydney lost her brother; she also lost her parents. Peyton has become their sole focus. They barely pay attention to her. It didn’t use to bother her, but it’s starting to make her feel very lonely. <br /><br />I absolutely believe Sarah Dessen has created some unforgettable characters here. Lovely Sydney is, of course, one of them, and so are all the new friends she has made changing schools. I appreciated the low amount of romance and the high focus on family and friendship relationships. <br /><br />While there is a love interest – who is good in every way – this isn’t about Sydney falling in love. It’s about her gaining confidence, becoming visible again in the eyes of her family and overcoming her fears. <br /><br />Sarah Dessen’s writing is majestic. Alright, maybe not, but I just really wanted to use that word, because I never get the chance to. She does write beautifully though, even if not necessarily poetically. She doesn’t write to impress or draw tears to our eyes; she writes to describe and create realistic settings. Although there are some heavy scenes that definitely stirred something inside me. <br /><br />Recommended. Go read now. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1299611353?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1299611353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6440777595313993010"><i>
  <b>"That’s the thing, though. You always think you want to be noticed. Until you are."</b>
</i> <br/><br/><b>My first ever Sarah Dessen read and I loved it!</b><br/><br/>It's kind of difficult to explain how I feel about this book by just using words. I don't even think I can give justice to this book through this review, because until now I'm still in a state of an emotional high.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23009402.Saint_Anything' title='Saint Anything by Sarah Dessen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Saint Anything</a> is <b>INCREDIBLY AMAZING!</b><br/><br/>I've just marked it as a new <b>favorite</b>, because it's hard not to. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2987.Sarah_Dessen' title='Sarah Dessen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah Dessen</a> has written something so powerful an</span>
  <span id="freeText6440777595313993010" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"That’s the thing, though. You always think you want to be noticed. Until you are."</b>
</i> <br /><br /><b>My first ever Sarah Dessen read and I loved it!</b><br /><br />It's kind of difficult to explain how I feel about this book by just using words. I don't even think I can give justice to this book through this review, because until now I'm still in a state of an emotional high.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23009402.Saint_Anything" title="Saint Anything by Sarah Dessen" rel="nofollow noopener">Saint Anything</a> is <b>INCREDIBLY AMAZING!</b><br /><br />I've just marked it as a new <b>favorite</b>, because it's hard not to. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2987.Sarah_Dessen" title="Sarah Dessen" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Dessen</a> has written something so powerful and heartfelt and a dozen other expressive adjectives that can’t even begin to adequately describe how great this book is. <br /><br />Saint Anything isn't a total romance and a common story you often encounter in a Young Adult contemporary book. It's deeper and a lot more emotional. It basically talks about family relationships, personal growth, tragedy/recovery, true friendship, and love.<br /><br />What made me admire this book was the writing style. Sarah Dessen has this eloquent, beautiful way with words that flow with enough sensitivity and understanding. All throughout the book, I felt the calming, comforting feels which is a rare thing that happens to me when reading a book.<br /><br />Everything in Saint Anything is captivating. It showcases <b>real life</b>-- the ups and downs, struggles, and joy we feel. It also has a well-plotted ending-- which I couldn’t imagine being any more perfect. I have to admit that after experiencing this emotional journey, I had sad and happy tears. This book will stay with me for a very long time!<br /><br />Rating: 5 Stars </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2489527092" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2489527092?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141361734" href="/book/show/24926018-saint-anything">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2489527092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9579982765676576652">this was only my second sarah dessen novel, but i think its safe to say that i am a becoming a fan of her style and stories. <br/><br/>theres just something so effortless about her writing. there is a nice, easy quality when it comes to the prose and the flow of the dialogue is quite natural. i think this is such an asset when it comes to the type of stories she tells, because the simplicity of the writing strips away any distractions and allows the reader to focus on the heart of the story in a very effe</span>
  <span id="freeText9579982765676576652" style="display:none">this was only my second sarah dessen novel, but i think its safe to say that i am a becoming a fan of her style and stories. <br /><br />theres just something so effortless about her writing. there is a nice, easy quality when it comes to the prose and the flow of the dialogue is quite natural. i think this is such an asset when it comes to the type of stories she tells, because the simplicity of the writing strips away any distractions and allows the reader to focus on the heart of the story in a very effective way. <br /><br />i loved being able to read about sydneys ability to adapt to a really trying situation and also how she was able to learn about herself and grow along the way. one of my favourite things was even though she admitted that she had changed and made new friends, she still understood the importance of those who were in her life before and didnt lose touch with her old friends. i thought that was really neat. <br /><br />and even though i enjoyed this, there were a couple of tiny issues that i wanted to briefly mention. as much as i loved the characters, they just felt very familiar. im pretty they could easily be swapped out and put in another sarah dessen novel and i wouldnt even be able to tell the difference. also, the ending felt a little rushed. there were so many complex issues discussed within the plot of this book and it felt like they were all resolved within the last chapter? just a little anticlimactic for considering the time put into reading this. <br /><br />overall, this was your standard YA contemporary filled with growth, friendship, romance, family, and everything in between! perfect for those looking for a light and easy read that has some depth to it!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

  <span id="freeText797160462497057570" style="display:none">FINALLY.<br /><br />I dedicated the year of our lord 2018 to a little thing called the “Sarah Dessen Reread Extravaganza.” I spent the whole year (by which I mean an absolute fraction of it) rereading Sarah Dessen books and reliving my youth in order to Prepare Myself for her by then newish release, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1846379020" rel="nofollow noopener">Once and For All</a>. <br /><br />It, uh. It did not go well.<br /><br />Which is fair, honestly. I should not expect myself at the ages of 20 and 21 to like the same things I did when I was 13. Because those things included “wearing 18 coats of mascara in a misguided attempt to resemble the characters of the television program Pretty Little Liars” and “the television program Pretty Little Liars.”<br /><br />Neither of which scream Refined Taste.<br /><br />However, I was still disappointed. Because I still love fluffy contemporaries (okay fine, I read them a lot. I do not love them often) and I love nostalgia. THIS BOOK.<br /><br />This one was my favorite when I first read it in 2015, at the ripe old age of 17, and it is my favorite now, still, to this day. It has everything I love in a contemporary. Slow-burn romance built from friendship. Friendship. Pizza, and in-depth descriptions of pizza. Summertime. Complicated family dynamics that are magically and completely resolved within 300 pages. Coming Of Age.<br /><br />This book is a dream and I have simply zero complaints.<br /><br />For complaints, see any other Sarah Dessen review I have written.<br /><br />Bottom line: YAY.<br /><br />--------<br /><br />sarah dessen came thru<br /><br />--------<br /><br />sarah dessen come thru</span>

<div id="review_1366991172" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1366991172" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=overrated-books">overrated-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1366991172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5205144414508733854"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “You really only fall apart in front of people you know can piece you back together.” </i> </b><br/><br/>This is my first <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2987.Sarah_Dessen' title='Sarah Dessen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah Dessen</a> book and if the author is a consistent writer, then judging by the way she wrote this novel, I could say that she is one of the most wonderful, wholesome YA writers out there. The narrative is very simple but endearing. It has something in it I can’t explain that makes you feel close to home. It isn’t trying to emotionally overwhelm you. It is simply just telling you </span>
  <span id="freeText5205144414508733854" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br /><br /><b> <i> “You really only fall apart in front of people you know can piece you back together.” </i> </b><br /><br />This is my first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2987.Sarah_Dessen" title="Sarah Dessen" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Dessen</a> book and if the author is a consistent writer, then judging by the way she wrote this novel, I could say that she is one of the most wonderful, wholesome YA writers out there. The narrative is very simple but endearing. It has something in it I can’t explain that makes you feel close to home. It isn’t trying to emotionally overwhelm you. It is simply just telling you a lovely story. There are more than four hundred pages to the book and that's kind of long for a YA contemporary novel but this didn't feel long at all. I was actually surprised it has already ended.<br /><br />The main character, Sydney, is genuine and relatable. She is what mainly gripped me to the story. I like how she is portrayed as a good girl through and through despite being constantly neglected by her parents. I also took note of the components of the entire story having this really strong connection with one another collectively putting across a unified, very significant meaning. Even the book cover is meaningful. There is the right amount of romance, suspense, and family drama which isn't the overwhelming kind. Finally, even though the plot was not designed to be intense as it mainly portrays how a young girl has lived in the shadows of her older brother whether what he did was good or bad, it was still a very absorbing read.<br /><br />It isn’t a perfectly written story. Like many YA contemporaries, you’ll find some issues (not really major) unresolved but I like how there were proper resolutions to the main conflicts that needed to be resolved. <br /><br />Thanks to Pearly for the recommendation. Check out her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1299611353?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">lovely review.</a></span>

<div id="review_1038802878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1038802878" />
    <a title="Madison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12935859-madison"><img alt="Madison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506830086p2/12935859.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1038802878?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madison" href="/user/show/12935859-madison">Madison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12935859-madison?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1038802878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18334030256561296432">Initial reaction:<br/><br/>WHAT??!!!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409240252ra/10952743.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I am beyond excited. This just made my <s>day</s> <s>week</s> <s>year</s> life.<br/><br/>I have been waiting for this news ever since Sarah published <a href='http://sarahdessen.com/3942/blog/abandoning-and-listening/' rel='nofollow noopener'>this blog post</a> entitled "Abandoning. And listening." where she said: <br/><br/><blockquote>I abandoned my book. I’m not a writer right now. But I am a mom and a wife and a daughter and hopefully a decent person. I am walking down my own mountain as the race, such as it is, continues on above me with great riders in the lead. I’ll get back to it someday. But for now, I’m foll</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText18334030256561296432" style="display:none">Initial reaction:<br><br>WHAT??!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409240252ra/10952743.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am beyond excited. This just made my <s>day</s> <s>week</s> <s>year</s> life.<br><br>I have been waiting for this news ever since Sarah published <a href="http://sarahdessen.com/3942/blog/abandoning-and-listening/" rel="nofollow noopener">this blog post</a> entitled "Abandoning. And listening." where she said: <br><br><blockquote>I abandoned my book. I’m not a writer right now. But I am a mom and a wife and a daughter and hopefully a decent person. I am walking down my own mountain as the race, such as it is, continues on above me with great riders in the lead. I’ll get back to it someday. But for now, I’m following my own path. One step at a time.<br><br>So there may not be a book from me right on schedule in summer of 2015. And now you know why. I’m not sure if it’s the best idea to share all this on the internet, basically rolling over and showing my soft, tender underside to anyone who peeks in. Admitting your failures is no picnic. But this space, this blog, has always been a safe one for me, and I wanted you, my friends and readers, to know why I might not tweet or blog as much for awhile. I need to rest. I think my book was trying to tell me that: it just took me a long time to listen. I’m listening now.</blockquote><br><br>Not being dramatic, I felt like my life as a reader was being totally crushed that day. It would be a similar to how one would have felt if you found out that they were not going to make the last Harry Potter movie. <br><br>ANGER*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409240252ra/10952744.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*but not at Sarah Dessen, because she is perfect and I could never be angry with her. Just anger at the "situation."<br><br>Then... <br><br>TEARS<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381146851ra/4373278.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And after that, I had to remind myself that it was just fiction. Just books.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409240252ra/10952745.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But books are wonderful.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409240461ra/10952793.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And these aren't just any books, and Sarah Dessen isn't just any author. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409240252ra/10952746.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So I will wait for Saint Anything in 2015 with bated breath, and I will be reading it as soon as it comes out:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1571265911ra/28305002.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Reaction after reading the book:<br><br>THANK GOODNESS!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380368212ra/720761.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was so worried that I was going to hate this. It's not that I've ever read a bad Sarah Dessen book, it's just that her past two weren't my favorite and I had my concerns. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431741175ra/14863830.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After reading the first reviews though, I grew more and more optimistic. I decided to just take the plunge and went straight for a hardback copy. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431741175ra/14863831.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Soon I was sucked into the world of Sydney. While not the most interesting of Dessen's leading females, she is one of the most relatable for me personally. There are a lot of similarities between Sydney and Auden from Along for the Ride, who I immediately related to as well. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431741175ra/14863832.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I appreciated that the main focus of this book was on personal growth. While most of her other books are too, they always share the limelight with romance storylines. Yes, there was a love interest, but it didn't take center stage. Instead there was a lot of inner reflection from Sydney's point of view.<br><br>Family drama. Sibling issues. Friendship struggles. Pressure in academics. <br><br>Check. Check. Check... and Check.<br><br>There was also a traumatic event that set everything into motion, one of which I can also sort of relate to not personally, but within my family and community. I liked how Sydney reacted to everything. It was realistic... awkward... tense... just as it should be. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413363494ra/11501649.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And in the midst of all that, Sydney reflected on how she never felt "seen." Again, something else I can relate to. Of course people saw Sydney, but not for who she really was, just what they wanted her to be. It took her new friends to show her that it's okay to love the root beer suckers that everyone else hates... (But really, do most people not like those? Because they're one of my favorite flavors too!)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431742810i/14863923._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>There were several similarities between Saint Anything and Dessen's previous books in terms of plotlines and character development, but was a little darker and more serious. There were still the telltale signs that it was a Dessen novel; however, it was just... <br><br>To best explain my feelings, I will take a direct excerpt from when Sydney's mom was trying out a new recipe: <br><br><blockquote>"Here goes nothing," she said, shaking some in. More steam rose up, followed by another blast as the curry powder hit. She poked at the vegetables with her spoon, folding them over once, then again. "What do you think?"<br><br>"It's a change."<br><br>"That it is." She tossed in some more cumin, then leaned in close, taking a long sniff, then gestured for me to do the same. Hesitantly, I did. It didn't smell bad or good. Just new. Different.</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431742810i/14863924._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>**Oh, and if you ever meet an "Ames" in your own life, tell him my fist says hi. What a creeper!**<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400107063ra/9635884.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="18334030256561296432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15218199478184554788" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <i>“There is a weird thing that happens when something goes from a one-time thing to a habit. Like the problem is no longer a temporary houseguest but has actually moved in.”<br></i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431090585i/14791127._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This story started out good, but then it just bombed.<br><br>I felt really sorry for Sydney in this story. Even though it was her brother who was a drug addict and had nearly killed someone, her mother acted like Sydney was the bad guy, and her brother Peyton was a saint! She didn’t even care that he had nearly killed someone, or that he was in prison, she acted like the whole thing was one big injustice, and she really annoyed me.<br><br><b>
  <i>“What was a fifteen-year-old doing out riding his bike at two in the morning anyway?”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431090585i/14791128.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline in this started out pretty good, and I thought that Layla, the girl that Sydney met at her new school was a really good friend, and I hoped that things would go well for Sydney. After the 35% mark though things went really downhill. The pace was too slow, very little of interest happened, and Sydney’s parent’s actually got worse!<br><br><b>
  <i>“I’m seventeen,” I told them. “I can stay alone for a weekend.”<br>“That’s not happening,” my mom told me. “I think we all know well what a lack of supervision can lead to.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431090585i/14791129.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There was a little bit of romance, but it didn’t appeal to me. When Sydney got a little bit interested in a certain boy I was just like ‘where did that come from?’.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Had I really just almost kissed him?”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431090585i/14791130.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending to this was okay, but I was pleased that the book had ended really. This book was so promising in the beginning, but it just lost its way, and lost my attention.<br>6 out of 10<br></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1664952358" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1664952358" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1664952358?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=best-covers">best-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1664952358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9326165918013438159"><i>Saint Anything</i> was a book I wasn't expecting a lot from. I've read a Sarah Dessen book before, and honestly, it just wasn't for me. I didn't fall into it and love the characters or even care about them after the book. So, as I write this review I've decided to lower my star rating to 2. That isn't to say I didn't enjoy this book because I did. I mean, the beginning even had me like <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464079003ra/19192123.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>and the side characters had me going <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380298456ra/684081.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>However, the story quickly went downhill for me. I mean, I stopped reading in </span>
  <span id="freeText9326165918013438159" style="display:none"><i>Saint Anything</i> was a book I wasn't expecting a lot from. I've read a Sarah Dessen book before, and honestly, it just wasn't for me. I didn't fall into it and love the characters or even care about them after the book. So, as I write this review I've decided to lower my star rating to 2. That isn't to say I didn't enjoy this book because I did. I mean, the beginning even had me like <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464079003ra/19192123.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and the side characters had me going <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380298456ra/684081.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However, the story quickly went downhill for me. I mean, I stopped reading in order to do my investigative report on koalas (don't ask). I mean, what does that say? I really felt that Sarah lost her grasp on the story as it continued, with extra plots falling in that weren't needed and just to make the characters go through more trials. This lead to me being completely underwhelmed around the 80% or so mark and wanting to slam my head against a wall. This meant that I honestly didn't care about the completely open ending. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470951844ra/19984847.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Characters</i><br><br><b>Sydney</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431968003ra/14887986.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Everyone, this is Sydney,” she’d announced the day after our talk when I finally gathered up the courage to accept her invitation to join her and her friends at lunch. “She transferred from Perkins Day, drives a sweet car, and likes root beer YumYums.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>The gif of Hermione I have used for this particular character, our main character, is completely representative of my feelings. I liked Sydney enough to clap for her, but she was boring enough that I have no reaction to it. I personally felt that Sydney had little to no personality. She was constantly doing what others wanted her too and whereas other characters had things they enjoyed doing <u>she did not.</u> <br><br>There was also the fact that she was passive as hell. What does this mean? She wouldn't stand up for herself. In any situation. She wouldn't even attempt to stand up for herself. She would try, once, and then stop altogether. Sydney didn't even tell her parents that she felt uncomfortable around her brother's best friend, who made me feel icky. It may just be because I have a close relationship with my mum but I would have told her instantly if that happened and she would make sure that person was no longer in our lives. I just hated Sydney's parents, but that's another story completely and I don't want to talk about it in this review. <br><br>Sydney had a thing about being invisible. I didn't get it, and Sarah didn't really write it too well. I mean, I just couldn't grasp <b>why</b> she was invisible. Because of her brother? I just felt it was an annoying plot line that only came up when Sydney needed reassuring she was pretty or something by Mac. <br><br><b>Mac</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474154171ra/20561958.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“The first time you came into Seaside,” he said. “You weren’t invisible, not to me. Just so you know.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>The point of Mac is obviously to be the love interest, but I would have preferred the book from his perspective. He was a lot more interesting than Sydney in the way that I could relate to him, I can't relate to people who tend to have a lot of things given to them (Sydney). I liked Mac. He was a great character, who was given a personality, unlike Sydney. However, I did prefer his sister Layla over him. That's a whole other review. <br><br>Mac was a great character in the fact that he brought light into Sydney's life. But, I found my annoyances. He was so conscious about his weight and what he ate, and everything he ate <b>had</b> to be mentioned which made this book tedious in some sense. I don't care that Mac is eating grapes or celery or crackers with hummus. What does this add to the plot? I personally thought he had an eating disorder and that would be a problem that rose, but no. He was a fat kid turned skinny. I can understand wanting to keep the weight off, but <b>why</b> was Sydney mentioning it every time he ate?! Then he ate a packet of chips and she told him <b>not</b> to? No thanks. <br><br>Despite how ranty I am getting, I did enjoy Mac as a character. His family was great. <br><br>Also, there's a merry go round behind the woods near his house. Do I want to say, how freaking random is that? The merry go round gets mentioned a total of about four times before it's forgotten. I honestly expected it to feature a bit more considering the fact <b>it's on the cover.</b><br><br>By merry go round I mean something like this, is it called something different if it has horses and all that?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474154892ra/20562023.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Plot</i><br><br>The plot, the big one, I didn't mind. This was because the romance wasn't at the forefront of everything. It took a backseat. But, mini plots kept popping up everywhere. Literally, everywhere. They added nothing to the characters and, in fact, kind of ruined them for me. <br><br><i>Writing</i><br><br>The writing felt disjointed. We were meant to know that Sydney liked Mac, and I think we got two sentences before they were kissing. That doesn't happen for a while in the book, but still. These characters showed no inkling of liking each other at all. That was the trend the book followed, random things happening without much explanation, or things moving way too fast to the point I was confused as to where that happened. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426589652ra/14058093.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Overall</i><br><br>Overall, this book felt slightly messy to me. Too much happened and not a lot of explanation was given for many things. Everything that could go wrong with these characters <b>did</b>. Now, a gif to round it all up. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474154892ra/20562024.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>EDIT:</b> there was communication in this book as well, which I loved. I forgot to say that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9326165918013438159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8503331919076936615">This is my first of Sarah Dessen novel,and I've heard so many great things from my friends about this author(especially from my friend PINKY),who also pushed me to read this and finished a lot more of Sarah Dessen.<br/><br/>The story is about a 17 year old young lady named Sydney Stanford(who came from a wealthy family),who is anguished with guilt over what his older brother(Peyton),<br/>did to a young bicyclist boy who he had severely injured in a drunk-driving accident,who is now on wheel chair.   <span id="freeText8503331919076936615" style="display:none">This is my first of Sarah Dessen novel,and I've heard so many great things from my friends about this author(especially from my friend PINKY),who also pushed me to read this and finished a lot more of Sarah Dessen.<br /><br />The story is about a 17 year old young lady named Sydney Stanford(who came from a wealthy family),who is anguished with guilt over what his older brother(Peyton),<br />did to a young bicyclist boy who he had severely injured in a drunk-driving accident,who is now on wheel chair. In short,Sydney is living in her older brother's shadow who is now serving his time in jail.<br /><br />The story also revolves around a creepy guy,a family friend of the Stanfords who I feared from Sydney's safety. I didn't like how her parents,especially her mom hardly even noticed the creepiness of this guy,and I hated how they ignored and neglected their second child. My heart really broke for Sydney because her parents' focuse is on her older brother notably now that he ended up in prison.<br /><br />The ending of this novel though,came a bit too easy,I felt like it was rushed that it disappointed me a bit.(I despise a story that ends abruptly),and it was kinda dragging but then,I did enjoy reading this.<br /><br />What I really liked here is the story about friendship,love,family and finding your self..that even no one notices you,you do feel that you exist,and accepted by new friends and by a warm and caring family that I found in Chatham family (a simple,but a happy family that I adored <br />so much,especially Layla,Mac and their mom).<br /><br />To my friend PEARL, thank you so much for recommending this to me..<br />To my friend PINKY, I would definitely read some more of SARAH DESSEN,to really know her so well through her writings.^^<br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1180137361" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1180137361" />
    <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks"><img alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577577052p2/3533262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1180137361?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey (prettybooks)" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141361734" href="/book/show/24926018-saint-anything">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1180137361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4505269623564415911"><em>Saint Anything </em>was the final book on my <a href='https://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2015/07/01/hooray-its-summer/' rel='nofollow noopener'>summer reads TBR</a> (even though I started it in September...) and I'm so glad it ended on a high. A novel about 'family, self-discovery and change', <em>Saint Anything</em> was a spectacular end to the summer.<br/><br/>Sydney feels invisible compared to her accomplished older brother Peyton, even when his rebellious behaviour ends in a tragic accident that leaves a boy in a wheelchair and Peyton with a prison sentence. Left feeling angry and guilty, Sydney can't understand why</span>
  <span id="freeText4505269623564415911" style="display:none"><em>Saint Anything </em>was the final book on my <a href="https://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2015/07/01/hooray-its-summer/" rel="nofollow noopener">summer reads TBR</a> (even though I started it in September...) and I'm so glad it ended on a high. A novel about 'family, self-discovery and change', <em>Saint Anything</em> was a spectacular end to the summer.<br /><br />Sydney feels invisible compared to her accomplished older brother Peyton, even when his rebellious behaviour ends in a tragic accident that leaves a boy in a wheelchair and Peyton with a prison sentence. Left feeling angry and guilty, Sydney can't understand why her parents only care about Peyton's well-being. To get away from being known only as his sister, Sydney starts a new school and stumbles into the chaotic life of the Chatham family. She becomes close friends with siblings Layla and Mac, who work in the family pizza place. As she spends more time with them, Sydney finally begins to explore who she is.<br /><br /><em>Saint Anything</em> may be sold as a contemporary romance story – the slow-building romance between Sydney and Mac <em>is</em> wonderful – but I adored watching Sydney discover who she is outside of her brother's shadow. Sydney constantly struggles with what Peyton has done. She is compassionate, thoughtful and feels guilty on behalf of her brother; she bears the weight of the world on her shoulders. Sydney wants to put everything right, but feels powerless to do so. Enter, the Chatham family.<br /><br />The Chathams are the sort of family we all wish we knew. Even though they barely know Sydney, they accept her straight away into their close-knit circle. It's here that Sydney finds support and discovers that even though the family has their own problems – from older sister Rosie's drug conviction to their mother's daily struggles with multiple sclerosis – they keep on going, and they'll happily take Sydney with them.<br /><br />It wasn't until I finished the book and was persuading <a href="http://snugglingonthesofa.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Debbie</a> to read it that we noticed how similar it was to <em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12294652.My_Life_Next_Door" title="My Life Next Door by Huntley Fitzpatrick" rel="nofollow noopener">My Life Next Door</a>
</em>, another summer read that I adored this year. But even though the stories may echo each other, they're both full of unique, colourful characters and have a very different feel to them. I adored both, and they're up there with my favourite young adult contemporary stories. Perfect for all seasons, <em>Saint Anything</em> is a brilliant story about one girl's determination to be herself.<br /><br /><i>Thank you to the publisher for providing this book for review!</i><br /><br /><i>I also reviewed this book over on <a href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Books</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4505269623564415911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1264952102" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1264952102" />
    <a title="Kristina Horner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3070540-kristina-horner"><img alt="Kristina Horner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425746408p2/3070540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1264952102?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristina Horner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristina Horner" href="/user/show/3070540-kristina-horner">Kristina Horner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3070540-kristina-horner?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1264952102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6062477267397897257">It had been a long time since I read a Sarah Dessen novel, but the cover on this one really caught my eye. I know, I know. Judging a book by its cover. But it's so pretty!<br/><br/>I was a bit torn on this book. I enjoyed it, but it was a little slow for me. There were a lot of characters to keep track of, and a lot of various different plotlines that I didn't feel added up to a whole. <br/>High school can be a tumultuous time even without your brother landing himself in prison, but I often felt like I wasn't </span>
  <span id="freeText6062477267397897257" style="display:none">It had been a long time since I read a Sarah Dessen novel, but the cover on this one really caught my eye. I know, I know. Judging a book by its cover. But it's so pretty!<br /><br />I was a bit torn on this book. I enjoyed it, but it was a little slow for me. There were a lot of characters to keep track of, and a lot of various different plotlines that I didn't feel added up to a whole. <br />High school can be a tumultuous time even without your brother landing himself in prison, but I often felt like I wasn't sure which plotline to care about the most. Sydney's relationship with her parents? With her old friends from her previous school? Her diminishing relationship with her brother? Her new relationship with the Chathams? The Chatham mom being sick? Layla's shitty boyfriend? The blink-and-you-miss-it issues with Eric's momentary crush on her? The Mariposa girl whose purpose only seemed to be pushing Sydney and Mac closer together? The fact that Ames was so creepy all the time, and Sydney never once tried to tell her parents? Rosi's issues? There was so much.<br /><br />I really did like the discussion of guilt and loneliness in this book, and thought both were executed quite well, but sometimes it just felt like there were too many plot lines to really focus on any one with significance. It felt like it was trying too hard to hit all the bases, when that just detracted from doing any of them justice.<br /> <br />Especially the whole symbolic saint thing. I actually really did like the concept of "Saint Anything", but Mac's necklace and the resulting yearning Syndey felt for wanting her own saint unfortunately felt very shoehorned in. I also wish the carousel had been in more than one scene, because it was cool, and that cover made me want to read this book in the first place.... and the fact that there's an ABANDONED CAROUSEL in the woods is deserving of more than one little midnight jaunt in the woods.<br /><br />Also I was constantly hungry while reading this book, and craved nothing but pizza and french fries for the duration of my reading of it. I think it lost a star simply for that. :P<br /><br />Anyway, I appreciated the important topics discussed in this book, but I wish she'd picked a couple and focused on them more. I think the Ames storyline could have used its own book. Same with Layla's boyfriend, and Sydney's obsession with David Ibarra. I just wanted more. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6062477267397897257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer16220150907701015499">Saint Anything is a perfect example of Sarah Dessen’s ability to pen a worthy Young Adult contemporary that’s filled with a great cast and a story that allows for a sense of connection.<br/><br/>In this novel, we meet Sydney who has always been overshadowed by her bigger-than-life older brother Peyton. Having the spotlight on him was the norm to her existence and that included her parents doting constant attention on him despite his transgressions. So when Peyton is charged with a drunk driving conviction</span>
  <span id="freeText16220150907701015499" style="display:none">Saint Anything is a perfect example of Sarah Dessen’s ability to pen a worthy Young Adult contemporary that’s filled with a great cast and a story that allows for a sense of connection.<br /><br />In this novel, we meet Sydney who has always been overshadowed by her bigger-than-life older brother Peyton. Having the spotlight on him was the norm to her existence and that included her parents doting constant attention on him despite his transgressions. So when Peyton is charged with a drunk driving conviction that leaves a fifteen year old boy paralyzed, Sydney finds herself lost and not quite sure how to adjust to the new family dynamics. She ultimately makes a drastic decision to switch from her small private school to Jackson High School to alleviate some financial pressure on her parents, and this is where she meets the Chatham family.<br /><br />Making new friends and redefining what’s important to her, Sydney finally gets a chance to feel a part of something and for once be noticed. The bond she creates with Mac and Layla opens Sydney’s eyes to true friendship and familial connection, which is always a good feeling to experience when reading one of Dessen’s novels. <br /><br />As with most of her other books, I absolutely love how Dessen doesn’t feel the need to make a romance the center of her books. She places more of an emphasis on friendships, family dynamics and character self-development, which was clearly evident in this book.<br /><br />The light romance between Mac and Sydney was fun to witness because it was so subtle, yet meaningful. I enjoyed their scenes together, but most of all I appreciated what they came to mean to each other. The saint charm he gave her was a nice gesture because I know how much something like that means to those that believe in protectors. Very heartwarming.<br /><br />Overall Saint Anything was signature of Dessen’s ability create a meaningful story about family and friends. I enjoyed this book from beginning to end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16220150907701015499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1145560831" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1145560831" />
    <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin"><img alt="Jaime Arkin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303353688p2/5293701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1145560831?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaime Arkin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaime Arkin" href="/user/show/5293701-jaime-arkin">Jaime Arkin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=galley-arc">galley-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=stand-alone-books">stand-alone-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=on-my-real-shelves">on-my-real-shelves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=viking-pub">viking-pub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293701-jaime-arkin?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1145560831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1189008863452062546">4.5 stars <br/><br/>I was trying to explain what I loved most about this book to my lovely friend Meg the other day… I knew when I struggled with that, that I was going to struggle with writing my review.<br/><br/>I rambled on about how I have only read a couple of Sarah Dessen’s books… I’d liked them but they weren’t anything that really stuck with me. <br/><br/>This however… this was different. <br/><br/>And I knew it was going to be different from the very first chapter. <br/><br/>Sydney… always admired her charismatic older brother, but as </span>
  <span id="freeText1189008863452062546" style="display:none">4.5 stars <br /><br />I was trying to explain what I loved most about this book to my lovely friend Meg the other day… I knew when I struggled with that, that I was going to struggle with writing my review.<br /><br />I rambled on about how I have only read a couple of Sarah Dessen’s books… I’d liked them but they weren’t anything that really stuck with me. <br /><br />This however… this was different. <br /><br />And I knew it was going to be different from the very first chapter. <br /><br />Sydney… always admired her charismatic older brother, but as they got older, his behavior became more concerning and more dangerous and ultimately leads to an accident and a jail sentence. While her parents focus on Peyton and what they can do to make his time in jail more tolerable, Sydney struggles with the guilt that she feels her family should instead be focusing on. Determined to start fresh, she transfers from the private school she attends to the local public school and tries to disappear in the flood of students who have no clue who she is or what her brother did. <br /><br />A random stop at a local pizzeria introduces her to Layla and Mac and the Chatham family… owners of the pizza place. <br /><br />The dichotomy of Sydney’s family to that of Mac &amp; Layla was reminiscent of that of Sam &amp; Jase in My Life Next Door, and I think that is part of what I loved about them so much. Where Sydney’s family is reserved and concerned about appearances, the Chathams are loud and messy and chaotic and so different than what she is used to. <br /><br />Ultimately this is Sydney’s story… her story of building friendships, hanging on to the ones that matter and finding new ones that are life changing. It’s about coming to terms with things in your past and finding the strength to create a future and of course there’s some romance… though that definitely takes a backseat in this story. <br /><br />I found it hard to put this book down once I started… the story itself isn’t an easy one. Sydney’s guilt for the things her brother did was understandable… the anger Sydney harbored for her brother was understandable… the irritation at her parents for their lack of care for the family of the boy who was injured was understandable, but I really wanted Sydney to stand up for herself a lot sooner than she did. I wanted her to make her mom see who she was and acknowledge how she had been neglecting her needs and her feelings in order to coddle her brother. <br /><br />I loved that the romance in this one took a back seat to the friendship for the most part. Layla and Sydney form an incredible friendship, one filled with bumps and bruises but when it comes down to it, they are there for each other no matter what. And while I say the romance takes a backseat, it’s still there. I loved the evolution of Mac and Sydney’s relationship because it was friendship first. Mac was such a wonderful leading man, his story was interesting and unique and a wonderful addition. Watching their friendship turn into something more was done so subtly and it was just lovely. <br /> <br />Dessen develops every character carefully and weaves them into the story… though I struggled a bit with the brother’s friend storyline, and why he was such a big fixture in Sydney’s mom’s life. That doesn’t mean it didn’t make sense… it’s just that parts of it didn’t work fully for me. I think we could maybe have done without it and the story would still have been amazing. <br /><br />Dessen’s Saint Anything is a story of grief, guilt and loneliness… but it’s also a story of finding yourself and forging your way. Definitely my favorite of hers! <br /><br />I could probably go on and on here, but I won't. I'll just say get this one as soon as you can and enjoy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1189008863452062546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
